bowmellobowmello encamped countrey ſerued wonderfull well arrangyng battailles large playnes paſſable horſes euery without ſtubbes ſhorte bruſhe couer ground withall ſo free proſpect eye might decerne thynges great waye appeared hilles within playne darius cauſed theſame caſte downe ground made ſmothe suche coniecture made reporte alexander darius power coulde credited could thinke ſo many ſlayne coulde greater power gathered together neuer doubted perill muche leſſe multitude men eleuēth encāping came riuer euphrates ouer whiche made brudges paſſed ouer horſemen afterwardes footemen mazeus ſent againſt ſix thouſand horſemen let paſſage durſt encoūter continued fewe dayes reſte ſouldiers alſo confirme myndes encourage ſette forewardes ſtoutly againſt enemy fearyng would haue retired back inwarde partes coūtrey whether ſhould haue bene enforced folowe waſte place deſertes therefore fourth daye paſſed arbella came vnto ryuer tigre countrey beyond ryuer ſmoke newely ſette fier mazeus burned thynges came euen bene enemy alexander fyrſte reaſon darcknes ſmoke ſtayed feare embuſhementes ſent ſcoure contrey reported thing clere apoynted fewe horſemen proue paſſage riuer founde deapnes fyrſt entre come horſe breaſte middes ſtreame horſe neckes riuer eaſt partes worlde ronneth ſo violētly beſides water riuers rōne driueth downe ſtones ſtreame ſo ſwiftnes called tigre whiche percian tonge ſo much ſay arrowe footemē therfore deuided two bādes holdīg armour ouer ther heades encloſed ſydes horſemen ſo paſſed till came deape chanell without anye great difficultye kinge firſte amonge fotemen paſſed ouer furtherſide hande ſeinge voyre could harde ſhewed ſhallowe place vnto ſouldiers muche paine kepe footing reaſon ſtones whervpon ſtumbled violence water toke feete ſpecially ſuch ware armour kinge ſaid take ſuertie neuer one appoynted ſhall refuce go thou ſhalt paſſecraterus done left craterus charge campe hym ſelf paſſed forwardes ſuche fotemen accuſtomed perſon thoſe hādes meleager chargemeleager thouſād archer horſback taking firſt ordre crateus ſhould kepe cāpe ſuch forme bene vſed cauſe many fiers made purpoſe yt enemy might yt rather think hym ſtil preſent aduiſing yt ariobarzanes ſhuld get knowlege enterpriſe ſend part powre ſtop paſſage yt thē craterus ſhould ſhew al ye terror could cauſe cōuert thē ſelf defence daunger yt next hand ſhould deceiue enemye recouer hil vpon hym vpon hearing alarome percians campe preparing thē ſelues reſiſtaūce ſhould doubt paſſe way wer repulced day wher iudged thei ſhould find reſiſtaunce enemy conuerted towards ye third watch ſet forwardes great ſilēce without blowyng trompet paſſed ſuch way ſhewed guide euery ſouldier lyght armed carieng thre dayes vitaile way beſides wild rockes ſharpe ſtones cauſed oft fayle foting ſnowe alſo driuen wyth wynd great impediment iourney fell diuers tymes downe pittes ſuche coueted pull oft time drawen night alſo wyth countrey vnknowne guide whoſe fidelitye doubted encreaſed muche feare conſidering • hat ſhould deceiue enemy watch ſhould taken like beaſtes wayed alſo ſauegard king lay handes one priſoner length came mounteyne wher way towards ariobarzanes lay right hād thē ſent guiding ſuch taken priſoners philotas cenon amintas policarpon wyth band lighteſte armed aduiſed foraſmuch horſemē fotemen coūtrey fertell habound fodder ſhould make haſte paſſe forwardes faire eaſely eſquiers body band horſemē called agema guided another bipath farre frō yt place wher enemy kept watch way ſo ſtreight ſo depe yt thei ſuffred great trouble vexaciō paſſing therof middaie ſo weried neceſſitie muſt take reſte ſo farre go trauailed redy ſauing waye ſo difficult ſo roughe refreſhed therefore men wt meat ſleape ſecōd watche riſe vp paſſed reſte hys iourney without great difficultie sauing ye part moūtayne begāne fall aſlope towards plaine paſſage ſodeinly ſtopped great gull made violence ſtreames ranne downe moūtains wearing away ye earth beſids tree ſtāding ſo thick bowes grewe one within another appeared thē cōtinual hedge whē ſaw thēſelues ſtaied maner ſuch deſperaciō fel amōges thē yt thei could ſ • arſly abſtain frō teares darknes great encreaſe terror ſeing thei could enioy benefit ye ſtatres gaue light ye ſame takē away ye ſhadow ye tree ye vſe eares could ſerue one receiue counſel comforte wynd whyrlid ſo amōges leaues ſhakyng bowes made ſuch noyſe length daie ſo much deſired demyniſhed wyth lighte terror darknes night make fetching little compaſſe paſſed holow gylle euery man began aguide finally got vp toppe hille whence might beholde enemy lieng campe thē macedon ſhewed ſelues ſtoutly armour appering ſodeinly backes miſtruſted ſuche thyng ſlewe ſuche came fyrſte encountre wyth one parte greuous noyſe ſlayne miſerable ſhowt ſuche ran ſuccour amonges owne companye put reſt flyght without making reſiſtaunce alarome hard camp wher craterus lay army paſſed forward go ſtreightes repulſed day philotas alſo policarpō cenos amyntas gone waye arriued ſame tyme gaue terror vnto enemy whē perciēs ſawe ther enemy agreing al partes ons though ſo oppreſt wyth ſodaine inuaſion fyrſt doubt yet length aſſembled githers fought notably neceſſitie ſtyring vp faintnes theyr harte oftentymes diſpaire cauſe mennes good hope vnarmed cloſed armed wyth weyght body drewe enemy earth killed diuers owne weapōs arriobarzanes fourty horſemen fiue thouſand footemē kept perſone brake battaill macedon great ſlaughter owne men enemy makyng haſte recouered perſepolis chief citie countrey excluded thence within renued againe fight ſuch ſo ſlayne ye time craterus made ſpede could deuiſe come vnto alexander fortefied campe theſame place diſconfite enemy though fled certaine victory yet becauſe found way ſtopped many place great deape diches thought good vſe circumſpection make ouer great haſte ſo muche feare enemy force nature ground whiche ſawe apt worke policie againſt hym paſſing forwardes houſes brydge made moment helpe ſtones whiche layde foundacion alexander paſſed riuer came nere vnto cytie company met ſo miſerable ſeldome haue bene found memory ſame grekes nombre iiii thouſande whome percians time taken priſoners afflicted diuers kyndes tormē te ſome feete cut ſome handes eares marked fleſh hote yrons whō percians mayming deforming maner kept reſerued amō ge memory deſpite towardes nacion thei ſawe yt ſhould become vnder obediēce another prince ſuffred grekes mete alexāder thei appeared rather image ſome ſtraunge mōſters mē nothing could decerned knowen voice compaſſion wretched eſtate cauſed beholder let fall fewer teares thēſelues could appeare whiche thē moſte miſerable though affliction diuers whē cried alexāder iupiter reuēger grece opened drue themſelues together conſult beſte demaūde alexander ſome opiniō aſke dwelling place within aſia others minde retourne vnto coūtreisentemeons oracion entemeon cimeus ſpake thus vnto euen nowe aſhamed ſhew heades priſon darkenes make ſuite aide relief become ſuch ſimplicitie preſently deſire ſhew vnto grece pleaſant ſpectacle infirmity maimes wherof haue much cauſe aſhamed ſorowfull muſt thinke ſuche beare miſeries beſt finde meanes hide moſte none ſo familier countrey mē vnfortunate ſolitarines forgetfulnes former eſtate whiche make accōpt frendes pitie compaſſion know howe ſone teares wil drie vp creature loue faythfully whome abhorre calamitie nature querelous ſo felicitie always proude euery one doth vſe cōſider fortune determineth man except bene myſery one v long ago bene wery meruayle though men infelicitie ſeke always equalies opinion therfore mē whiche long ago dead lyfe ſeke v place wherein may hyde maymed member exyle may hyde horryble ſcarres ſhall retourne vnto countrey beyng caſe cannot vngrateful wyues maried young ſhall chyldren ſhall brother acknowledge v beyng priſon ſlaues though thynges ſhould ſuccede would wyſhe yet ſmall nombre v able trauayll ſo many countreys howe poſſible v banyſſhed vttermoſte bondes orient aged impotent maymed ſuffre thoſe thynges whiche haue tyred men force victorious axed ſhal become wyues whome chaunce neceſſitie hathe gotten vnto v comforte priſonement ſhall child haue begotten take v leue behinde v returne ſuche haue none thoſe grece acknowledge v ſhall ſo madde leue thoſe comfortes haue already vncertayne whether ſhall come thoſe ſeke verely muche better v hyde ſelues amonges whiche haue bene acquainted v myſery theſe eutemon wordestheatus wordes theatus athens reaſoned contrary creature qd whome remaineth ſparke goodnes eſteme v outward ſhape ſeyng calamitie come nature deſeruyng miſfortune enemy crueltie ſuche aſhamed fortune chaunſes well worthy ſuffer miſaduenture geue greuous ſentence vpon eſtate man mortalitie diſpaire muche mercy deny cōpaſſion mē miſery therfore ſince goddes haue offered thing whiche ye durſte neuer haue wiſſhed countrey wiues childrē thinges whiche men eſteme lyfe redeame oftentymes death doubt enioymēt thē breake impriſonemēt iudge yt yet countrey moſte naturall v thīkes maner beholding ye light cuſtomes religiō another maner tonge whiche ye pleaſaūtnes coueted barbarous naciōs great thinges therfore thoſe ye would willingly leaue ye wāte ye cauſe miſery opiniō plain yt viſite countrey home refuſe ſo great benefite alexander hath proffered v ſo deteined loue ſuche wife child haue gotten ſeruitude let ſuche impedement others al thinges eſteme moſte naturall countrey opiniō cuſtome greater force nature preuailed matter agreed demaunde alexander would geue vnto ſome place inhabite choſed hundred ſuters vnto hym behalfe whome alexander perceiued coming towardes hym thynking would haue required thing conceiued minde haue apointed qd beaſtes cary euery one denires ſhal come grece wil ſo yt excepting miſfortune ſhall thinke themſelues better caſe ſawe loke ſtill towardes ground neither lifted vp countenaūces ſpeake enquired cauſe heuines eutemon rehearſed thoſe thinges effect ſpoken coūſel king therfore pitieng leſſe demaunde miſfortune cōmaunded iiim deneres geuen euery one garmentes beſides ſhepe cattell corne wherby might till ſowe lande ſhould appointed vnto next day aſſembled captaines army togethers ſhewed thē citie enemy grekes ſame chief ſeage aunciēt kinges perce whence great army bene ſent grece howe darius firſt xerxes come place moue vniuſt warre againſt europe deſtruction whiche cytie thought good reuenge predeceſſours thinhabiters abandoned citiethe taking perſepolis fled feare dyd driue thē wherupon king ſtreight wayes brought footemen ſpoyle therof time wonne many city ſome force ſome compoſicion full ſubſtaūce prince treaſure ryches citie excide reſt place perciās layd whole ſubſtaunce gold ſiluer foūd heapes great plenty ryche veſtures furnimentes houſes neceſſitie neceſſary vſe exceſſe oſtentacion whiche ſo great gaue victourers occaſion fight amonges ſelues eche takyng enemy gotten rycheſt ſpoyle plenty ſuche could employe vſe ryches found ſawe thynges value eſtemed rather toke away till ſuche time euery one couetyng haue parte euery thyng tare brake ſonder princely robe precious veſſels curious workemanſhip image gold ſyluer either beaton gobetes plucked peces euery one caught holde nothing left vntouched nothing caried away whole crueltie bare leſſe rule couetouſnes euery one ſo laden gold ſiluer eſteamed keping priſoners kylled ſuche firſt ſpared hope gayne many therefore preuented enemy handes voluntary death diuerſe clothyng ſelues moſte precious apparell leaped downe walles wyfes chyldren certayne ſet owne houſes fyer whiche iudged enemy woulde el haue done ſhortely becauſe would burne themſelues amunges owne family length kyng dyd horſemen band footemen without bagage went viſite winter ſeaſon inward partes perce vexed troubled ſhoures tēpeſtes yt maner intollerable yet letted go forwardes enterpriſe ye place yt appointed iourney came vnto coūtrey yt couered ſnowe theſame alſo froſen force could wildnes deſert maner therof put ſouldiers weried trauail inſuch feare terror imagened haue ſene vttermoſte boūdes world beheld thinges waſt ſigne appearing habitaciō man amaſed made requeſte returne againe light elementes ſhould fail king would chaſtice terror leped frō horſe went one fote ſnow ice thing whē frēdes ſawe could ſhame folow captaines like finally ſouldiers kyng firſt breake ice made ſelfe away whoſe enſample reſte folowe length hauing paſſed woodes without way thei foūd ſome appearaunce habitacion perceyued flockes ſhepe thinhabitours dwelled cotages diſparcled aboutes ſawe men cōming whome iudged enemy thinking bene encloſed ſlew ſuch able folowe fledde wild mountain ful ſnowe length cōmunicatiō ſuch toke priſoners wildnes ſōwhat mitigated yelded ſelues alexander whō hurted kind way whē deſtroied parte perce brought townes vnder obediēce came ye coūtrey ye warlike mardōsthe mardons whiche differed much frō reſt ye percians maner liuing wiues child dyd inhabite within caues mountaines liued wyth fleſhe ſhepe wyld beaſtes ye womē according kind appearaūte mekenes mildnes thē men either theyr perſonages diſpoſitions curled heere hang vpon face garmentes came knee band theyr ſlinge fyllet forhead whyche vſed ornament defence nacion al vncyuill rude maner could eſcape ſubdued ſame force fortune yt others xxx daie departed perſepoles returned thither againe gaue rewardes fredes al reſte according deſeruing diſtributing maner al rich found within cytie al excellēt vertues mind princely quality wherin excelled al kinges conſtancy al daungers perilles yt celeritie deuiſing perfourming enterpriſes promis keaping towards yt yelden clemēcie towardes priſoners tēperaūce lawful accuſtomable pleaſures defaced intollerable deſire delite drinking notwithſtanding enemie cōtended thempire chiefly prepare warres gathering powre togethers though people newly cōquered receiued quiet ſubiection yet gaue ſelfe continually feaſting banqueting wher womē euer preſēt ſuch whō mē reſpect honeſtie harlotes whiche libertie beſeming cōpany men warre amonges thē ther one thaysthays vpō daie dronkenes affirmed alexāder ſhould wonderfully winne fauor greakes would commaund palaice perſepoles ſet fire diſtruction wherof ſhe ſaid greatlie deſired forſomuch ſame chief seate kinges perce tymes paſte diſtroyed ſo many great city whē dronken harlot giuen hir ſentence preſent likewiſe drōken cōfirmed hir wordes alexander enclinacion heate pacience ſaid whi reuenge greace ſet citie fire al chaffed drinking roſe immediatly vpon thoſe wordes burne citie dronkennes men warre ſpared fury king ſelf firſt geſtes ſeruauntes concubine ſet fier palaice builded moſte parte cedre tree became ſodeinly flame army encamped nere vnto citie ſaw fire thought ben kendled ſome caſualty came ronning quench ſame thei ſawe king ther preſent noriſhing fire powred downe water brought healped likewiſe matter forwardesthe diſtrucion perſepoles thus palaice hedde whole orient whence ſo many nacions fetched lawes liue vnder ſeate ſo many kinges yt terror ſomtyme grece ſame hath bene ſender forth nauies x thouſand ſhippes army ouerflowed europe made bridge ouer sea vndermined mountaines ſea hath nowe hys courſe cōſumed eand neuer roſe againe age enſue kinges macedon vſed city parthian handes deſtruccion citie ſuch foundacion thereof daye coulde found riuer araxes doth ſhew ſtode diſtant frō perſepolis xx furlonges inhabitātes rather beleue knowe macedon aſhamed ſo noble cytie deſtroyed king hys drōkenes yet length turned earneſte matter content thynke expedient cytie ſhould haue bene deſtroyed maner certeine alexander taken reſte become better aduiſed repented hym ſayed percians ſhould haue doone greakes harme ben chaunce haue reigned xerxes ſted next daie gaue xxx talentes rewarde guide perce thence toke iourney mediamedia new ſupplie ſouldiers plato athens conduccion came cilicia vc fotemē thouſand horſemen whē meanes encreaſed powre dettermined purſue dariusecathana come ecathana hedde citie medium purpoſed thence haue paſſed bactria fearing preuented ſpede enemy made altered purpoſe iourney alexāder come nere hym amvc forlōg could think diſtāce ſufficiēt defend againſt celeritie therfore prepared ſelf rather fight fle wt xxxm footemen amōgs whō ther iiiim grekes whoſe fidilitie neuer failed al aduers fortūe alſo iiiim archer slinger beſides iii thouſand iiic bactrian horſemen vnder beſſus charge gouernour ye citie bactria contrey darius band wythdrue litell highe waye commaundyng verlets ſuch charge caryng paſſe beforedarius wordes called counſell ſpake theſe wordes vnto fortune matched cowardes ſuche eſtemed kynde lyfe honeſt death would rather haue holden peace conſume wordes vaine haue greater experience would wyſhe valiaunt courage fidelitie towardes parte ought rather labour ſeme worthy haue ſuche frendes doubte whether ye yet remaine theſame men towardes ye ſo many thouſandes vnder myne empire thoſe haue folowed ſticked haue bene twyſe ouerthrowen field twyſe enforced flye away fidelitie conſtancy maketh thinke remayne ſtill kyng traitours fugitiues reigne cyties thought worthy ſuche honour myght prouoked rewardes reuolte againſt notwithſtanding haue choſen rather folowe miſfortune partaker victorers felicitie worthy whome goddes ſhall reward may vndoubtedly wyll poſteritie ſo ſilent fame ſo vngrateful ſhal due cōmendaciōs extolle ſterres though determined ſtill haue fled whereūto harte neuer agreed yet haue conceyued ſuche truſte vertue man hode purpoſe paſſe againſt myne enemy howe long ſhall baniſſhed within myne dominion ſtraunge forein prince flye within boundes myne owne kingdome may haſarding battaill either recouer haue loſte el dye honeſt death except peraduenture ſemeth better ſome mē ſhould ſubmit myſelf enemy thenſample mazens mithrenes receiue peticion dominion ſome one nacion wherin iuge alexander rather folowe thinclinacyon glorie hys wrath let god neuer graunte may lye man powre eyther take awaye gyue vnto thys deadeame vpon hede loſe impire ſo longe remaine liue determined breath kingdome ſhall end togither mynd remayne thys lawe graffed harte none want libertie non ſhalbe cō pelled endure vrkeſomnes enemy neither proud porte ſtately lokes euery man ryght hand ſhall giue vnto hym ſelf either reuenge end thes euils nothing ſtand long one ſtay ſelfe enſample alteracion fortune without cauſe loke better change worſt fall god wyll neds againſte v warres lauful honeſte yet cannot taken v may alway manfully honeſtly dye require make interceſſion honor predeceſſors ſuche fame glory poſſeſſed kingdomes hole orient thoſe mē whō macedon ſometyme tributarie ſo many nauies ſhips ſent grece ſo many victory wonne ye wyll take ſuche courage hart vnto may ſeme worthy nobilitie nacion ſame conſtancie minde wherwith ye haue endured thinges paſte ye wyll proue attempte ſoeuer chaunge ſend hereafter reſolued part get ſelf perpetual fame either victorie notable aduenture giue wynning therof darius ſpoken theis wordes repreſentacion preſent perill ſo amaſyd able either ſhew aduiſe ſpeake worde matterartabazus til ſuch tyme artabazus moſte auncient frendes tyme bene wyth king philip began ſay hys fancie come felde qd king moſte precious apparell richeſt armoure▪ entent win victorie neſſeſſitie require refuſe death whoſe wordes reſte ther voice ſeamed agre sauing nabarzanes preſent counſell wyth beſſus hys opynion conſpired treaſō ſo wonderful like hath ſeldome ben hard determinacion force ſouldiers vnder charg put ther kinge hold wyth purpoſe alexander purſued deliuer aliue hādes wynne therby fauor thing thought would eſteame greatly coulde eſcape conueniently mynde kyll darius deuiding kyngdome betwixt renue againe warre againſte macedon hauing imagened treaſō long mind nabarzanes thoughte occaſion make preparatiue wicked intent perſuaſion vtterednabarzanes wordes knowe qd ſhall ſpeake thing firſte apparaunce ſhall grateful vnto eares pheſicions vſe cure deſeaſes greate ſharpe bitter medycines ſhipmaiſters whē fear ſhipwrack accuſtume redeame ſuch thinges may ſaued diſtruction loſſe reſte thys matter meane parſuaſion loſſe deuice meanes ye may preſerue ſelf kingdome make warre wherin god ſeme manifeſtly againſt v fortune ceaſeth obſtinatly purſue v nedefull therfore lay new foūdacions ſeke men haue fortune opinion therefore deliuer vp kingdom vnto ſome mānes hādes ſhal haue name king ſo longe enemy remaine within aſya departed minde geueth ſhortly ſhal reſtore ſame vnto againe countrey bactria yet vntouched indian saeans apointement ſo many people ſo many armes ſo many thouſandes horſemen fotemē haue force redines renue warre yt muche greater force remaineth yt cōſumed like beaſtes wilfully runne diſtruction neceſſary ye ꝓpertie ſuch men courage rather diſpiſe death hate life oftentymes werines trauayll towardes driuen take little regarde ſelues vertue leaueth nothing vnprouided death beynge ende thynges ſufficient god yt lyke ſluggardes therefore ſhal go vnto bactria next refuge let v time ſake make beſſus king alredy ruler ye countrey whē ye matter brought ſome ſtaie ſhal reſtore thempire againe righteouſe king although darius ꝑceiued ye greatnes miſchief laye hidden vnder hys wicked wordes yet meruaill though could obſtayne turned towardes ſaid thou vile ſlaue haſt thou found time mete diſcloſe treaſon lyeth thy harte therwyth pulled hys ſworde haue ſlaine beſſus ſtraight waye come bactrians letted purpoſe pretendyd ſory matter mindid dede bind continued purpoſe meane ſeaſon nabazzanes eſcaped away beſſus folowed imedialy dyd aſſault therof whē came bare ſteape rock ye labour ſemed waſte nature wrought againſt diſpoſiciō alwayes ſtriue agaynſt difficulty conſideryng howe hard matter go forwardes daungerous returne backe agayne caſte head wayes deuiſes could imagined nowe fanteſied one thing men wont whē way haue found firſt pleaſe ſtode ſtay doubt doe fortune miniſter vnto meane neither wit reaſon could inuente chaunſed wynde blewe ſore ſouthweſt tyme ſouldiers felled great plenty wood wherof thei thought make ſelues away vp againſt rocke heat ſonne made theſame drye alexander perceiued wynd blowe ſorte woode lieng place cōceiued purpoſe willed tree cut downe laid vpō putting thinges apt kyndle noryſhe fier tree heaped vpon tree became mountaine ſo hyghe top rocke ſame ſet fire al partes wynde caried flambe face enemy ſmoke couered ouer ſky noiſe great fier made burned tree fired purpoſe alſo reſt woode growing nere enemy ſo tormented flambe heate fire enforced forſake place ſtrength fledde india thus lien campe nyne dayes alexander without feare enemy inuincible againſte foren power brought perill treaſon peoplea treaſon cō ſpired againſt alexand chaūſed one dymnus mā meane fle away heare deſertes beſkorned greake prouerbes couet rather deſertes place vnhabited city plentiful countres therefore hold thou thy fortune faſt ſhe ſlipper cannot kept agaynſt hir wyll folowe thou counſell yt good ſpecially whilles tyme doth ſerue put bridle thy felicitye thou ſhalt gouerne better ſaye fortune without feete ſhe hath hand winges whē ſhe putteth furth hand ſhe wil ſuffre hir winges touched thou god geue benefites vnto mortal men take away commodity haue alredy thou man conſidre alwaye thine owne eſtate foliſhe remembre thoſe thynges cauſe forget thy ſelfe suche warre thou makeſt thy enemy peace thou maiſt make thy veray frendes moſt firme frēdſhip amōgeſt equal ſeme equall haue yet made trial ther force take hede thou take thy frendes thou doeſt ſubdue bring remayning haue eſcaped thy crueltye attalus philotas parmenio lynceſtes alexander clytus nowe deade ennemyes behoue alyue ſtode fyghte defended ſwordes receyuing woundes thy glory victory whome thou diddeſt ſie thine enemy attalus put death without iudgement thus thou vſeſt thy handes v wretch inſtrumentes one kill another thou diddeſt make thy tormentours alitle ſtraightwayes thou commaundeſt tormented others thoſe wordes multitude began ſhout againſt harmolaus father drewe ſworde purpoſe haue ſlaine bene letted kyng whiche cōmaunded harmolaus ſpeake required reſt heare paciently whiche ſaid enforced cauſe puniſhemēt lēgth great labour thei held peace harmolaus began liberall ſuffre rude child ſpeake voice caliſtenes ſhut vp priſon becauſe alone able tell tale becauſe thou feareſt freſpeche innocent becauſe thou canſt endure behold face yet iuſtifie priuy matter purpoſed noble enterpriſe accuſe caliſtenes conſent yet thou art pacient rightuous king haſt determined death theſe rewardes macedon whoſe bloud thou doeſt miſuſe vile valeur thou haſt xxxm mule carieng ſpoyle treaſure yet poore ſouldiers cary nothing vnrewarded woundes ſkarres thinges eaſely ſuffre thou diddeſt betray v barbarous newe trade victourers make v ſlaues thou alloweſt apparell diſciplyne percians deſpyſeſt maners thine coūtrey therfore determined kil king macedō kyng perce fugitiue perſecuted lawe armes thou wouldeſt haue macedōs knele worſhip god thou doeſt refuſe philip thy father god bene iupiter thou wouldeſt haue refuſed likewyſe doeſt thou maruaille free men beare thy pryde hope thy handes ſeyng muſte either dye innocentes el worſe death lyue remayne boundage ſlaues thou arte greatly debte thou couldeſt amende thou haſte begunne learne thyng free harte cannot endure spare whoſe cruelty againſt yt durſt obiect towardes couetouſnes wil cal witnes one one leſt ſhuld braide wt liberalitie making declaraciō haue beſtowed vpon behold ye whole multitude litle ago nothing el bare thē reigne proudely ouer ſuche haue ſubdued came aſia vtterly ſubuert naciōs make one half worlde deſert geue cōquered cauſe repent victory occaſion gladly fight kyngdome ſpend bloud proudly vſed ſhal make empire ſtable perpetuall truly haue nowe well wyſhe deſire couetouſnes vnſaciable thyng ſpecially men deſire fill veſſell ronneth ouer ye ſaye myxe brynge cuſtomes amonges ſo whie becauſe ſee diuers nacions right many thynges whiche nede aſhamed folowe ſo greate empire haue gotten cannot otherwiſe aptly gouerned except deliuer ſome thynges thē receiue likewiſe ſome one thing laught ſhould refuſe iupiter father ſo acknowledged oracle ſaith anſwere god power proffered ye name ſōne vnto vnmete ye thinges purpoſed woulde wiſhe yt indian beleued god ye ſucceſſe warre ſtand much fame faulſely beleued ſomtyme worketh theffect thinges true geue exceſſe prodigalyte bicauſe garniſhed armor gold ſiluer purpoſe ſhewe men accuſtumed nothing vile ſuch kynd mettell declare macedōs frende death thes two ſo hardy yonge men▪ reſte moued alexander greatly yet parceyuing remedy ye matter cauſed retracte ſowned gretly ſalfgard▪ retired lettle little without aperaunce anye feare greatnes ſubdued ninth boke quintus curtius actes great alexander kyng macedon alexander reioyſinge ſo notable victorye wherby ſawe confines ye orient opened vnto hym offred vp ſacrifice vnto sunne alexander builded citye vpon either ſide riuer hidaſpys whyche perfourmed gaue euerye one capitaynes crowne golde thouſand piece golde beſides preferryng rewardynge euery accordynge qualitie degree deſeruyng abyazares whyche ſent embaſſadours vnto alexdnder battayle fought wyth porus ſent embaſſadours agayne offeryng thynges woulde appoynt ſo kepe bodye libertye deſiered lyue except myght
